VERTICAL AND CURVE WELL EVALUATION
QEP Energy Company
Moberg 20-21-29-28LL
Figure 1: Unit Rig #121 on the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL, Dec. 2014 - Jan. 2015.
INTRODUCTION
QEP Energy Company's Moberg 20-21-29-28LL [SW SW Sec. 20, T149N, R95W] is located
approximately 25 miles southeast of Watford City, North Dakota. The Moberg 20-21-29-28LL
is proposed as a double section 9,580' lateral targeting the Three Forks Formation within Grail
Field of the Williston Basin. This lateral will be drilled to the east within sections 20 and 21. The
Moberg 20-21-29-28LL is the second of two wells on the pad to be drilled to completion.
OFFSET WELLS
Primary offset wells used in correlation with the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL, were QEP Energy
Company's Moberg 3-20-21TH, Moberg 2-20-21TH, both located within 1,250' to the
northwest, and QEP's Moberg 4-20/21H also located north of the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL.
These offset wells provided useful information including very similar isopach and interval
thicknesses. This information helped to determine relative projections and illustrations when
drilling the vertical, and building an accurate curve. Once more all offsets were expected to
provide reliable data as they too were drilled into the Three Forks Formation.
OPERATIONS
The Moberg 20-21-29-28LL was spud on January 2, 2015 by Unit Drilling Rig #121. Previously
a 13 ½" hole was drilled with fresh water to 2,128' MD, and isolated with 9 5/8" casing
cemented to surface. Once the surface hole was completed, the drilling fluid was changed to
diesel invert for the vertical and curve. The vertical hole was drilled to our kickoff point for the
curve build at 10,551' MD. Halliburton provided all tools, directional, and MWD personnel.
GEOLOGY
Methods
All geologic personnel and analysis for Moberg 20-21-29-28LL was provided by Sunburst
Consulting, Inc. The gas, rate of penetration, and all other drilling parameters were delivered via
Pason's electronic data recorder system. Total gas was measured in units, using a 10,000 unit
scale. Beginning at 7,500' MD, rig crews caught lagged samples at the direction of the well site
geologists. Samples were collected at 30' intervals throughout the vertical and curve. Two sets of
dry cuttings were collected for QEP Energy Company, one of which was sent to the North
Dakota Geological Survey. Rock cuttings were analyzed in wet and dry conditions under a
20x60 power binocular microscope.
Prospective Intervals
The Mission Canyon Formation was 587' in thickness. The upper section varied from lime
wackestone to mudstone and contained dark brown algal laminations with fair amounts of
anhydrite throughout the formation. The middle to lower sections primarily consisted of
argillaceous limestone described as firm mudstone,
light gray to tan in color with an earthy texture. The
Mission Canyon did show traces of light brown oil
staining primarily in the lower half of the
formation. Background gas throughout the
formation remained between 100 to 200 units. Gas
units throughout the Mission Canyon remained
unusually low with relation to similar wells in this
area, whereas there were no discernable gas shows
above 200 units.
The Upper Bakken Shale was 22' of soft to friable
sub-blocky and petroliferous black shale. This
shale has a consistent distribution of disseminated
pyrite within the rock. The Upper Bakken Shale
high gamma signature and abundant oil shows are
Figure 2. Upper Bakken Shale.
distinguishing characteristics. Although the formation was entered at around 55°, and were only
exposed for roughly 36' MD, gas was recorded at 1,600 units on average, with a peak of 2,572
units.
The Middle Bakken was 41' in thickness. The upper portion of the Middle Bakken consists most
notably of silty sandstone. This upper facies was described as being medium gray, in parts dark
gray. It is also soft, with calcareous cement, showing common spotty brown oil stain. The lower
portion of this silty sandstone emits a high gamma signature in relation to surrounding rock, and
is mostly consistent throughout the Middle Bakken. Underlying the silty sandstone is a variable
1' to 4' thick limestone interval consisting of a hard, light gray packstone, commonly containing
laminated algal material and fossil fragments. The lower facies is defined as a light to medium
gray-brown silty sandstone. It ranges from fine to very fine grained, and consists of calcareous
cement, poor intergranular porosity and traces of light brown oil staining. Background gases
here remained consistently between 600 and 1,200 units, with a gas peak at 11,058' MD reaching
to 1,251 units.
The Lower Bakken Shale was drilled for 30' TVD, and almost 80' MD. This shale was dark
brown to black, sub-blocky, with an earthy texture. It is also carbonaceous and highly
petroliferous. Background gases throughout the Lower Bakken Shale averaged 1,500 units with
one significant peak at 11,193' MD of 1,842 units.
Three Forks target
The target zone within this Three Forks lateral was set
at 20' thick. The top of the target window starts at the
"hot" gamma ray marker, or approximately 12' below
the Lower Bakken Shale. This high gamma ray
signature consists of light blue to green shale with
traces of interbedded dolomite, and creates a signature
marker for position affirmation within and near the top
of target.
Curve/Landing
The kick off point to start the curve build was reached
at 10,551' MD on January 06, 2015 while drilling in
the Lodgepole Formation. The landing was proposed to
be 20' TVD into the Three Forks Formation. The TVD
Figure 3. Shale and dolomitic siltstone
within the Three Forks Target Zone.
landing was not adjusted during the curve due its close
relativity to the expected formation tops. The curve was successfully drilled with one BHA that
landed on January 08, 2015 at 06:40 CT within the target zone, 21' TVD into the Three Forks at
11,044' TVD. Upon completing the curve, 7" 32# HCL-80 intermediate casing was set and
cemented from 11,358' MD to surface.
SUMMARY
This vertical and curve portion of the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL well was drilled to completion
with a high level of confidence based on the solid data from the prior Three Forks well already
finished on the pad. As the data indicates, not many changes to the prognosis were needed. It is
always ideal to have such closely related data to reference when building and landing a curve.
As was the case here, the projected landing was not altered from our prognosis. Although data
suggests the curve was landed fairly low within the target zone, this once again most often gives
valuable information as to the overall gamma signatures that will be seen within our zone.
Respectfully submitted,
Al en Gilbert
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
January 10, 2015
LATERAL WELL EVALUATION
INTRODUCTION
The Moberg 20-21-29-28LL is proposed as a double section 10,000' lateral targeting the Three
Forks Formation within Bear Den Field of the Williston Basin. This lateral will be drilled from
west to east within sections 20 and 21. The Moberg 20-21-29-28LL will be the second Three
Forks lateral drilled and completed on the pad.
ENGINEEERING
Prior to drilling the lateral, drilling fluid was changed from diesel invert to salt water. The entire
lateral was drilled using one BHA with no failures. The Moberg 20-21-29-28LL lateral was
completed on February 03, 2015 at 18:00 CT which reached a total depth of 20,927' MD and
11,112' TVD in 14 drilling days. The bottom hole location is 104.18' S & 9,687.75' E of surface
location or approximately 125.82' FSL & 250.63' FEL, SE SE Sec. 21, T149N, R95W. Overall
the lateral was drilled 99% within the target zone.
GEOSTEERING
The lateral section of the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL was geo-steered by the QEP Geology team.
Dip expectations were provided by QEP along with structure maps and nearby offset wells, all of
which suggested an approximate 0.26° regional structural down dip. Attempts were made to
correlate repeating gamma signatures for dip calculations. The two prominent markers used for
steering were the Hot Gamma Marker at top of target zone and Massive Dolomite at the bottom.
Both markers were encountered during the lateral section providing strong anchor points for geo-
steering decision making. The hot gamma ray signature at the top of target consists of blue shale
with traces of interbedded dolomite, while the Massive Dolomite creates a very low gamma
signature and consists of cream to tan colored, soft argillaceous dolomite. Initially a 0.26°
structural down dip was assumed from surface to bottom hole, however the dip in the beginning
of the well was different than expectations due to the turn drilling up an anticline. The overall
structure was very close to QEP's pre-drill estimation, only slight adjustments were made
throughout. The gross overall dip for the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL was 0.40° downward.
TARGET ZONE
The target zone defined by QEP was a 23' target window measured by 20' above the "Massive
Dolomite" and 3' below. Samples collected throughout the lateral spanned two facies, the
primary facies defined by QEP as the "Laminated Section" consisted of thinly interlaminated
shale and dolomite. Shale samples often fluctuating from light blue to light green, varying from
sub-blocky to sub-platy, typically calcareous and firm with interbedded dolomite. The dolomite
samples were described as: varying from tan to brown in color, soft to firm and sub-blocky with
pyrite inclusions consistently present. The "Massive Dolomite" facies was described as cream to
tan colored dolomite, very soft and argillaceous with an abundance of unconsolidated quarts
grains. These two rock facies as previously described remained fairly consistent throughout the
lateral.
Figure 1: Light green shale and tan dolomite in the lower portion or target window.
Color and pyritic density variations of the rocks help to determine stratigraphic positioning
throughout the lateral. Often higher concentrations of pyrite as well as dark striations within the
rock are noted near the top of zone, while lighter or more colorful samples are found near the
lower to bottom half of the target.
Background gas consistently increased throughout the lateral when the base of the target zone
was entered. Upon entering the lower quarter of target zone, gas typically increased by 2,000 to
4,000 units where gas shows peaked as high as 8,000 units.

SUMMARY
The overall gas units as noted were significantly higher near the bottom of target zone.
Throughout the target zone, spotty brown to light green oil staining was present within the rock
cuttings, as well as noticeable oil indications over the shakers. The lateral was drilled from
Intermediate Casing Point to Total Depth in 5 drilling days for a total of 14 drilling days from
spud to finish and reached TD at 20,927' MD on the 3rd of February, 2015.
Overall the Moberg 20-21-29-28LL was drilled approximately 99% within the designated target
zone, and shows great potential for oil production.
Respectfully submitted,
Eric Peters
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
February 04, 2015

LITHOLOGY
Moberg 20-21-29-28LL
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A
detailed list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma
ray marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were
examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Sample descriptions begin in the Spearfish
Formation. Diesel invert drilling fluid was used for the vertical and curve while Water based
drilling fluid was used for the lateral portions of the well.
7500-7530 SILTSTONE: orange, light organic, friable to firm, microcrystalline to sub-platy, moderately cemented,
calcareous cement, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; common ANHYDRITE, light cream, no visible porosity,
no visible oil stain; occasional SALT: clear, microcrystalline, hard, crystalline texture, anhedral, trace subhedral, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain
7530-7560 SILTSTONE: orange, light organic, friable to firm, microcrystalline to sub-platy, moderately cemented,
calcareous cement, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; occasional ANHYDRITE, light cream, no visible
porosity, no visible oil stain
7560-7590 SILTSTONE: red orange to light orange, friable, microcrystalline to sub-platy, moderately cemented,
calcareous cement, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; common ANHYDRITE, light cream, no visible porosity,
no visible oil stain; occasional SALT: clear, microcrystalline, hard, crystalline texture, anhedral, trace subhedral, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain
7590-7620 DOLOMITE: mudstone, tan to cream, microcrystalline, friable, dense, earthy texture, sucrosic texture,
trace intercrystalline porosity; SILTSTONE: light orange, light gray, friable, microcrystalline to sub-platy,
moderately cemented, calcareous cement, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; occasional ANHYDRITE, light
cream, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
7620-7650 SILTSTONE: red orange, friable, microcrystalline to sub-platy, moderately cemented, calcareous
cement, trace sandy grained, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; ANHYDRITE: off white, cryptocrystalline,
soft, amorphous texture, massive, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; occasional
7650-7680 SILTSTONE: red orange, friable, microcrystalline to sub-platy, moderately cemented, calcareous
cement, no visible porosity or oil stain

Well File # 29451
Dear Meghan:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24405, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement shall be located
approximately down the east-west axis (within 250' of the section line per Commission policy) and no closer than
200 feet to the east or west boundary within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 20, 21, 28, & 29
T149N-R95W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. QEP ENERGY CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Joyce Kohut at 701-202-1288 prior
to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 9738' east.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Meghan M Campbell
September 18, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

NOTES ON 9-5/8" SURFACE CASING DESIGN:
The key point in designing surface casing is to extend the shoe of the surface casing beyond the top of
the Pierre Shale. This ensures that all potable or usable water zones are covered. At this point in the well
design, the drilling fluid is changed to oil base mud to contend with salt sections that occur at
approximately 7,000' TVD and 9,375' TVD. The 36 ppf J55 casing accomplishes these criteria easily.
A higher burst rating is not necessary based on industry standards throughout the Williston Basin.
In the event the surface casing burst rating was increased, the normally pressured and sub normally
pressured zones all the way thru the Madison Group at approximately 8,750' TVD has the potential to
break down. Therefore the increased pressure rating of surface casing is not warranted. It is not feasible
to set the surface casing point at a greater depth because the shut in surface pressures would not
appreciably increase. The Dakota formation (5,350' TVD) is frequently weak. Typically, we drill the
intermediate section with 10.5 ppg OBM to the 7" casing point. In the event we lost circulation in the
exposed intermediate interval, the wellbore will not be entirely evacuated and the surface casing can be
shut in without compromising the pressure rating of the 36 ppf J-55.
Calculations for the Surface Casing Design:
3,520 psi/ (6,013 psi (Reservoir Pressure) ­ (11,013 ft x 0.22 psi/ft)) = safety factor of 1.0
Centralizers for 9-5/8" Casing
· (3) Bow Spring centralizers on the bottom 3 joints of casing

Cementing Program
16" Conductor:
Cement to surface with construction cement.
9-5/8" Surface Casing: 0' ­ 2,100' (MD)
Lead Slurry: 0' ­ 1,600'. 448 sxs (1330 cu ft) Varicem System (VariCem W1, is Type III cement with
the following additives: 2% BWOC Cal-Seal (accelerator), 2% BWOC Econolite (lightweight additive),
0.3% BWOC Versaset (Thixotropic), 6% BWOC Salt) + 0.25 lbs/sk Poly-E-Flake (LCM) Slurry wt:
11.5 ppg, Slurry yield: 2.97 ft3/sx, Mix fluid: 18.15 gal/sx, Slurry volume: 13-1/2" hole + 70% excess.
Tail slurry: 1,600'- 2,100 207 sxs (416 cu ft) Varicem System (see above - The lead and tail are
identical in composition, density is adjusted with water) + 0.25 Poly-E-Flake (LCM) Slurry Wt: 13 ppg.
Slurry yield: 2.01 ft3/sx, Mix fluid: 11.02 gal/sx, Slurry volume: 13-1/2" hole + 70% excess.
7" Intermediate Casing: 2,100' ­ 11,316' (MD)
Lead Slurry: 2,100' ­ 6,500'. 465 sks (860 cu ft) Econocem System (EconoCem W12, is a 25/50
poz/Class G blend (25% of a 79 lb sack of poz and 50% of a 94 lb sack of cement) with: 25 % Silicalite
(lightweight additive), 0.2% BWOC SA-1015, HR-601 (retarder, as needed) w/ 0.7% HR-5 (Retarder),
0.6% BWOC D-Air 5000 (de-foamer)) w/ 0.125 lbs./sx Poly-E-flake (LCM) Slurry wt: 12.0 ppg, Slurry
yield: 1.85 ft3/sx, Mix fluid: 10.40 gal/sx, Slurry volume: 8-3/4" hole + 30% excess.
Tail Slurry: 6,500' ­ 11,316'. 605 sks (950 cu ft) Extendacem System (ExtendaCem W13, is a 50/50
poz/Class G blend with: 15% BWOC SA-1015, 20% BWOC Silicalite (lightweight additive), 0.3%
BWOC D-Air 5000 (de-foamer), HR-5 (retarder, as needed) w/ 0.26% HR-5 (Retarder), 0.2% BWOC
Super CBL, and 0.125 lbm/sk Poly-E-Flake Slurry wt: 14 ppg, Slurry yield: 1.57 ft3/sk, Mix fluid: 6.47
gal/sx, Slurry volume: 8-3/4" hole + 30% excess.
VariCem, EconoCem and ExtendaCem are Halliburton trademarked products.

9.
Anticipated Abnormal Pressures and Temperatures, Other Potential Hazards
No abnormal temperatures or pressures are anticipated. No H2S has been encountered in or known to
exist from previous wells drilled to similar depths in the general area. Maximum anticipated bottom
hole pressure equals approximately 6,013 psi. Maximum anticipated bottom hole temperature is 290° F.
10.
Additional Information For Oil Base Mud
A. Oil-base mud will be mixed in the closed circulating system and transferred to 500-bbl tanks on
location for storage prior to and after drilling operations. Drip pans will be installed below the
rotary beams on the substructure and can be viewed on site from the cellar area. As the intermediate
and production section of the hole is drilled, the cuttings transported to the surface with the drilling
fluid will be mechanically separated from the drilling fluid as waste by shale-shakers and then
cleaned/dried via a mud cleaner and/or centrifuge. These separated cuttings will be transferred to a
container, dried and stabilized, and then transported to an approved disposal site or, if a cuttings pit
is approved, the solidified and dried cuttings will be stored in the pit.
B. Plastic material will underlay the rig, oil base mud/diesel storage tanks and mud pits. All tanks on
location will be placed inside of berms. Any oily waste fluids and sediments generated at the work
site during drilling operations or when cleaning the fluid containment system after drilling will also
be stabilized and then transported to an approved disposal site or, if a cuttings pit is approved, it will
be solidified and stored in the cuttings pit.
C. All rig ditches will be lined and directed to a lined sump for fluid recovery. A drip pan will be
installed on the BOP stack, a mud bucket will be utilized as needed on connections and a vacuum
system will be used on the rig floor for fluid recovery in those areas.
Page 6 of 8
ONSHORE OIL & GAS ORDER NO. 1
QEP North Dakota Operations
Moberg 20-21-29-28LL
D. If a cuttings pit is deemed necessary and acceptable due to unforeseen circumstances and/or
complications with the disposal method described in 10.A above, drill solids and excess cement will
be placed in the cuttings pit and the oilfield waste management consultant Soli-Bond (or a similar
company) will mobilize equipment and personnel to the site to perform the cement based
solidification/stabilization process in-situ for encapsulation with cement kiln dust or flyash prior to
placement in the cuttings pit. Once the drilling operation is complete, the lined cuttings pit will be
reclaimed to grade elevation.

COMPASS 5000.1 Build 65
Gas Capture Plan (Moberg 13-20Y2 Pad ­ 2 wells)
1. Affidavit: attached as a part of this gas capture plan.
2. Detailed gas gathering pipeline system location map
Oneok Rockies Midstream ("OKRM")
Oneok existing trunkline
Name and Location of gas processing plant: Garden Creek Plant, Section 35-T151N-R98W.
Name of gas gatherer and location of lines for each gas gatherer in the vicinity: OKRM 16" poly
highlighted in red; contracted with OKRM until 2019, no other viable gatherers in the vicinity.
Proposed Route and Tie-in point for wel connection: See above gathering system map
3. Detailed information for Blue Buttes/Grail/Sandstone compression capacity (circled in blue):
Maximum current daily capacity: Total: 95 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 35; Grail: 0) Note: Grail
station expected to start-up in mid-September 2014.
Current throughput: Total: 82 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 22; Grail: 0) Note: Grail station
expected to start-up in mid-September 2014.
Anticipated daily capacity at date of first gas sales: Total: 130 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 35;
Grail: 35).
Anticipated throughput at date of first gas sales: Total: 130 MMcfd (Sandstone: 60; Blue Buttes: 35;
Grail: 35).
Gas gatherer issues or expansion plans for the area: Beginning September, 2014, OKRM has adequate
pipeline, processing plant and compression capacity for QEP's current and forecasted gas through mid-
2015. These midstream facilities were designed to handle approximately 70 MMcfd of QEP's gas.
Should future iterations of QEP's volume forecast exceed 70 MMcfd, QEP will require another OKRM
expansion for compression and pipelines and has alerted OKRM of this possibility.
4. Detailed flowback strategy:
Anticipated date of first production: 2nd Quarter, 2015
Anticipated oil and gas rates and duration (total for all pad wells): See table below.
Moberg 13-20Y2 Pad
Compl. Date Q2 of 2015

5. QEP flaring amounts:
Statewide percentage of gas flared for existing wells in the Bakken petroleum system: 53% for the most
recent month of July 2014 (28.0 MMcfd flared /52.5 MMcfd produced).
Field wide percentage of gas flared for this well: 64% in the Grail field for the most recent month of July
2014 (26.6 MMcfd flared/41.5 MMcfd produced).
6. QEP Alternatives to flaring:
Specific alternative systems available for consideration: When OKRM is at capacity or not connected,
QEP has considered and implemented JT conditioning skids for its flaring wel s. QEP has done this on 2
pads in Sections 33 & 35 of T149N-R95W (vendor Montana-Dakota). QEP also is looking at site usage for
a number of applications to include powering wellhead equipment, drilling rigs, gas lift, etc. Further,
QEP is installing gas-powered generators on our pads in the Mandaree field (FBIR) instead of using diesel
fuel (second half of 2014).
Details of flaring reductions if such alternative plans are implemented: No significant flaring reductions
have been achieved from our implemented or planned alternative systems thus far. However, the
Montana-Dakota JT skids do reduce our VOCs by 85% where they are installed.
